Mike:
is asking if the Arduino will automatically start running the sketch again when he unplugs it and plugs it back in somewhere else (the barn). The answer is yes - once you upload a sketch to an Arduino, it's stored in the microcontroller's flash memory. Every time the Arduino powers on, it automatically runs whatever sketch was last uploaded to it. No computer needed after the initial upload. Simple, direct answer. Yes. Once the sketch is uploaded, it's stored in the Arduino's flash memory permanently. Every time it gets power, it runs automatically ‚Äî no computer needed. Mike:
is asking whether the piezo should be wired in series (in line) with the coil, or in parallel. For driving both with the same Arduino tone output, they should be wired in parallel - both positive leads to Pin 9, both ground leads to GND. This way they both receive the same signal. In series would divide the voltage between them and likely not work well or at all. Parallel. Both share the same pin: Coil ‚Üí Pin 9 and GND Piezo ‚Üí Pin 9 and GND Same two points, both connected. The standard way to seat it on a breadboard is: Straddle the center channel/gap of the breadboard so the pins on each side go into separate columns This way the pins don't short together Let me give him a quick, direct answer. Straddle the center channel. The breadboard has a gap running down the middle. Your phone stores rotation in EXIF, not the actual pixels. Your ESP-32 Arduino core is version 3.x ‚Äî they changed the API. Updated code for new ESP-32 core: cpp const int COIL_PIN = 25; const int LED_PIN = 2; const float FREQUENCY = 528.0; const int LEDC_RESOLUTION = 8; void setup() { pinMode(LED_PIN, OUTPUT); ledcAttach(COIL_PIN, FREQUENCY, LEDC_RESOLUTION); ledcWrite(COIL_PIN, 127); } void loop() { digitalWrite(LED_PIN, HIGH); delay(100); digitalWrite(LED_PIN, LOW); delay(1900); } What changed: ledcSetup() removed ‚Äî no longer needed ledcAttachPin() ‚Üí ledcAttach(pin, freq, resolution) ledcWrite() now takes the pin directly, not channel Paste this and upload again. LM317s + 18V Milwaukee batteries = clean, adjustable DC supply for the XY-PWM module and coil drive. The XY-PWM1 needs **7‚Äì30V** to run happy (higher voltage = stronger output swing for the coil). ### Quick & Dirty 18V ‚Üí Adjustable Supply with LM317 **Parts you need from your bag:** - 1x LM317 (TO-220 package is fine) - 2x resistors (for voltage set‚Äîe.g., 240Œ© and 1k‚Äì5k pot, or fixed values) - 1x heat sink (clip-on or improvise with aluminum) - Input/output caps if you have them (10¬µF+ electrolytic good) **Basic LM317 circuit** (current up to ~1A, plenty for coil): Milwaukee 18V (+) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ IN LM317 OUT ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ (+) to XY-PWM power input | ADJ | Resistor network | Milwaukee GND (‚Äì) ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ (‚Äì) to XY-PWM GND **Voltage formula**: Vout = 1.25 √ó (1 + R2/R1) - R1 = 240Œ© (fixed) - R2 = pot (0‚Äì5k) or fixed resistor Examples: - R2 = 1k ‚Üí ~6.5V - R2 = 2.2k ‚Üí ~12V (good sweet spot for XY-PWM) - R2 = 3.9k ‚Üí ~21V (max drive, but watch heat) **Build steps**: 1. Heat-sink the LM317 (it'll drop 18V ‚Üí 12V = 6W heat at 1A). 2. Wire as above. 3. Test no-load voltage first. 4. Power XY-PWM from OUT/GND. 5. Share GND with ESP32 if controlling. **Alternative: Direct 18V (if XY-PWM tolerates it)** Many clones run fine on 18V‚Äîconnect Milwaukee direct to XY-PWM power terminals (watch polarity). Coil gets max kick. **Coil drive tip**: XY-PWM output is square wave‚Äîgreat for strong magnetic pulse. Set 528 Hz, 50‚Äì70% duty, ramp current slow to avoid kickback. Dec 18, 2025
Mike:
is asking about how a MOSFET/transistor works. This is a clarification question about electronics, not a research task. He wants to understand the logic of the circuit to troubleshoot. He's asking about how a MOSFET works - but he's using a TIP120, which is actually a Darlington transistor, not a MOSFET. Let me clarify this. A TIP120 is a bipolar junction transistor (BJT), specifically a Darlington pair. It works differently than a MOSFET. BJT (TIP120): Current-controlled device. A small current into the BASE allows a larger current to flow from COLLECTOR to EMITTER. It's like a current amplifier - you put a little current in the base, and it allows a proportionally larger current to flow through. MOSFET: Voltage-controlled device. When voltage is applied to the GATE, it creates an electric field that allows current to flow from DRAIN to SOURCE. Very little current flows into the gate itself. Mike's description of "pressure switch" is closer to how a MOSFET works (voltage = pressure, and when it reaches threshold, current flows). But the TIP120 he's using needs actual current flow into the base. The key issue: The XY-PWM output might not be providing enough current through the 1kŒ© resistor to turn on the TIP120 properly. Let me explain this clearly without being condescending. Close, but TIP120 is a transistor, not a MOSFET. Different. TIP120 (Darlington transistor): Current-controlled. You push a small current INTO the base, and it allows a much larger current to flow from collector to emitter. Like a valve you open by pushing water into a small pipe. MOSFET: Voltage-controlled. Apply voltage to the gate, electric field opens the channel. Almost no current flows into the gate ‚Äî just voltage "pressure." Your TIP120 needs actual current into the BASE to turn on. The 1kŒ© resistor limits how much current the XY-PWM can push into the base. Mike:
is confused about how the circuit works. He thinks the transistor is "after" the coil and doesn't understand how frequency gets applied. Let me explain this clearly. The circuit is: +12V ‚Üí Coil ‚Üí TIP120 Collector ‚Üí Emitter ‚Üí GND The TIP120 is like a gate at the END of the path. When the gate opens (signal on base), current flows through the whole path. When gate closes, no current flows. The coil is "before" the transistor in terms of the current path, but the transistor controls whether current flows at all. Think of it like a faucet at the end of a hose. Water pressure (voltage) is always in the hose, but nothing flows until you open the faucet (transistor). Open and close the faucet 528 times per second, and the water pulses 528 times per second through the whole hose. Let me explain this simply without being condescending. Think of it like a light switch. The power line goes: +12V ‚Üí COIL ‚Üí TRANSISTOR ‚Üí GND The transistor is at the END, like a light switch on the wall. The wires go through the light bulb first, THEN to the switch, THEN to ground. When switch is OFF: No current flows anywhere. Coil sees nothing. When switch is ON: Current flows through the ENTIRE path ‚Äî through the coil, through the transistor, to ground. The XY-PWM flips that switch 528 times per second. So even though the transistor is "after" the coil, it controls whether current flows through the coil AT ALL. Flip it on-off-on-off 528 times per second, and the coil gets pulsed 528 times per second. The frequency isn't "put on" the coil like painting it. The frequency IS the switching.
